**Tool:** read
**Timestamp:** 2026-03-28 17:53:32

```
use std::sync::Arc;

use tokio::sync::{broadcast, mpsc, oneshot};
use tokio::task::JoinHandle;

use crate::agent::AgentHandle;
use crate::budget::BudgetTracker;
use crate::error::SupervisorError;

use super::child::ChildSpec;
use super::config::SupervisorConfig;
use super::event::SupervisorEvent;
use super::runner::SupervisorRunner;

pub(crate) enum SupervisorCommand {
    StartChild {
        spec: ChildSpec,
        reply: oneshot::Sender<Result<AgentHandle, SupervisorError>>,
    },
    StopChild {
        name: String,
        reply: oneshot::Sender<Result<(), SupervisorError>>,
    },
    GetChild {
        name: String,
        reply: oneshot::Sender<Option<AgentHandle>>,
    },
    Shutdown,
}

/// Cloneable handle for sending commands to a running supervisor.
///
/// All operations go through a bounded `mpsc` channel, so the handle
/// is safe to share across tasks. Dropping every clone of the handle
/// causes the supervisor to drain its children and exit.
#[derive(Clone)]
pub struct SupervisorHandle {
    command_tx: mpsc::Sender<SupervisorCommand>,
    event_tx: broadcast::Sender<SupervisorEvent>,
}

impl SupervisorHandle {
    /// Starts a supervisor with no token budget.
    pub fn start(config: SupervisorConfig) -> (Self, JoinHandle<Result<(), SupervisorError>>) {
        Self::start_with_budget(config, None)
    }

    /// Starts a supervisor with an optional shared [`BudgetTracker`].
    pub fn start_with_budget(
        config: SupervisorConfig,
        budget: Option<Arc<BudgetTracker>>,
    ) -> (Self, JoinHandle<Result<(), SupervisorError>>) {
        let (command_tx, command_rx) = mpsc::channel(32);
        let (event_tx, _) = broadcast::channel(config.event_capacity);
        let runner = SupervisorRunner::new(config, command_rx, event_tx.clone(), budget);
        let join = tokio::spawn(runner.run());
        let handle = Self {
            command_tx,
            event_tx,
        };
        (handle, join)
    }

    /// Returns a clone of the event broadcast sender.
    pub fn event_sender(&self) -> &broadcast::Sender<SupervisorEvent> {
        &self.event_tx
    }

    /// Spawns a new child from a [`ChildSpec`] and returns its handle.
    pub async fn start_child(&self, spec: ChildSpec) -> Result<AgentHandle, SupervisorError> {
        let (tx, rx) = oneshot::channel();
        self.command_tx
            .send(SupervisorCommand::StartChild { spec, reply: tx })
            .await
            .map_err(|_| SupervisorError::SpawnFailed("supervisor shut down".into()))?;
        rx.await
            .map_err(|_| SupervisorError::SpawnFailed("supervisor dropped reply".into()))?
    }

    /// Cancels a running child by name.
    pub async fn stop_child(&self, name: &str) -> Result<(), SupervisorError> {
        let (tx, rx) = oneshot::channel();
        self.command_tx
            .send(SupervisorCommand::StopChild {
                name: name.into(),
                reply: tx,
            })
            .await
            .map_err(|_| SupervisorError::SpawnFailed("supervisor shut down".into()))?;
        rx.await
            .map_err(|_| SupervisorError::SpawnFailed("supervisor dropped reply".into()))?
    }

    /// Looks up a child's handle by name, or `None` if it doesn't exist.
    pub async fn child(&self, name: &str) -> Option<AgentHandle> {
        let (tx, rx) = oneshot::channel();
        self.command_tx
            .send(SupervisorCommand::GetChild {
                name: name.into(),
                reply: tx,
            })
            .await
            .ok()?;
        rx.await.ok()?
    }

    /// Subscribes to [`SupervisorEvent`]s.
    pub fn subscribe(&self) -> broadcast::Receiver<SupervisorEvent> {
        self.event_tx.subscribe()
    }

    /// Sends a shutdown command; all children are drained.
    pub async fn shutdown(&self) {
        let _ = self.command_tx.send(SupervisorCommand::Shutdown).await;
    }
}
```

use std::collections::HashMap;
use std::future::Future;
use std::pin::Pin;
use std::sync::Arc;
use std::time::Duration;

use tokio_util::sync::CancellationToken;

use mra::agent::{AgentBehavior, AgentCtx, AgentReply, AgentSpawn, Task};
use mra::budget::BudgetTracker;
use mra::config::AgentConfig;
use mra::error::{AgentError, LlmError};
use mra::llm::{LlmProvider, LlmRequest, LlmResponse};
use mra::supervisor::{ChildContext, ChildSpec, SpawnedChild, SupervisorConfig, SupervisorHandle};

struct EchoBehavior;

impl AgentBehavior for EchoBehavior {
    async fn handle(&mut self, _ctx: &mut AgentCtx, input: Task) -> Result<AgentReply, AgentError> {
        Ok(AgentReply {
            task_id: input.id,
            output: input.instruction.clone(),
            self_tokens: 0,
            total_tokens: 0,
        })
    }
}

#[tokio::test]
async fn spawn_new_creates_working_agent() {
    let spawned = AgentSpawn::new("echo", EchoBehavior).spawn();
    let reply = spawned.handle.execute(Task::new("hello")).await.unwrap();
    assert_eq!(reply.output, "hello");
    spawned.handle.cancel();
    spawned.join.await.unwrap();
}

#[tokio::test]
async fn spawn_with_cancel_token_is_respected() {
    let cancel = CancellationToken::new();
    let spawned = AgentSpawn::new("echo", EchoBehavior)
        .cancel(cancel.clone())
        .spawn();

    cancel.cancel();
    let result = tokio::time::timeout(Duration::from_secs(2), spawned.join).await;
    assert!(result.is_ok(), "agent should exit when cancel token fires");
}

#[tokio::test]
async fn spawn_with_peers_enables_delegation() {
    struct DelegateBehavior;
    impl AgentBehavior for DelegateBehavior {
        async fn handle(
            &mut self,
            ctx: &mut AgentCtx,
            input: Task,
        ) -> Result<AgentReply, AgentError> {
            let echo = ctx.peers.get("echo").unwrap();
            let reply = echo
                .execute(Task::new(format!("via: {}", input.instruction)))
                .await?;
            Ok(AgentReply {
                task_id: input.id,
                output: reply.output,
                self_tokens: 0,
                total_tokens: 0,
            })
        }
    }

    let cancel = CancellationToken::new();
    let echo = AgentSpawn::new("echo", EchoBehavior)
        .cancel(cancel.clone())
        .spawn();

    let delegator = AgentSpawn::new("delegator", DelegateBehavior)
        .peers(HashMap::from([("echo".into(), echo.handle.clone())]))
        .cancel(cancel.clone())
        .spawn();

    let reply = delegator.handle.execute(Task::new("hi")).await.unwrap();
    assert_eq!(reply.output, "via: hi");

    cancel.cancel();
    echo.join.await.unwrap();
    delegator.join.await.unwrap();
}

        Box::pin(async {
            Ok(LlmResponse {
                content: "mock reply".into(),
                prompt_tokens: 10,

use std::collections::HashMap;
use std::time::Duration;

use mra::agent::{AgentBehavior, AgentCtx, AgentReply, AgentSpawn, Task};
use mra::config::AgentConfig;
use mra::error::AgentError;
use tokio_util::sync::CancellationToken;

/// A simple behavior that echoes the instruction back as output.
struct EchoBehavior;

impl AgentBehavior for EchoBehavior {
    async fn handle(&mut self, _ctx: &mut AgentCtx, input: Task) -> Result<AgentReply, AgentError> {
        Ok(AgentReply {
            task_id: input.id,
            output: input.instruction.clone(),
            self_tokens: 0,
            total_tokens: 0,
        })
    }
}

/// A behavior that sleeps for a fixed duration before replying.
struct SlowBehavior {
    delay: Duration,
}

impl AgentBehavior for SlowBehavior {
    async fn handle(&mut self, _ctx: &mut AgentCtx, input: Task) -> Result<AgentReply, AgentError> {
        tokio::time::sleep(self.delay).await;
        Ok(AgentReply {
            task_id: input.id,
            output: format!("done after {:?}", self.delay),
            self_tokens: 0,
            total_tokens: 0,
        })
    }
}

#[tokio::test]
async fn test_agent_execute() {
    let cancel = CancellationToken::new();

    let spawned = AgentSpawn::new("echo", EchoBehavior).cancel(cancel).spawn();

    let task = Task::new("hello world");
    let reply = spawned.handle.execute(task).await.unwrap();
    assert_eq!(reply.output, "hello world");

    spawned.handle.cancel();
    spawned.join.await.unwrap();
}

#[tokio::test]
async fn test_agent_shutdown() {
    let cancel = CancellationToken::new();

    let spawned = AgentSpawn::new("echo", EchoBehavior).cancel(cancel).spawn();

    let deadline = tokio::time::Instant::now() + Duration::from_secs(5);
    spawned.handle.shutdown(deadline).await;

    // JoinHandle should complete within a reasonable time
    let result = tokio::time::timeout(Duration::from_secs(2), spawned.join).await;
    assert!(result.is_ok(), "agent task should complete after shutdown");
}

#[tokio::test]
async fn test_agent_cancel() {
    let cancel = CancellationToken::new();

    let spawned = AgentSpawn::new("echo", EchoBehavior).cancel(cancel).spawn();

    spawned.handle.cancel();

    let result = tokio::time::timeout(Duration::from_secs(2), spawned.join).await;
    assert!(result.is_ok(), "agent task should complete after cancel");
}

#[tokio::test]
async fn test_agent_backpressure() {
    let cancel = CancellationToken::new();

    let spawned = AgentSpawn::from_config(
        AgentConfig::new("slow").with_mailbox_size(1),
        SlowBehavior {
            delay: Duration::from_millis(100),
        },
    )
    .cancel(cancel)
    .spawn();

    let handle1 = spawned.handle.clone();
    let handle2 = spawned.handle.clone();

    let t1 = tokio::spawn(async move { handle1.execute(Task::new("task1")).await });
    let t2 = tokio::spawn(async move { handle2.execute(Task::new("task2")).await });

    // Both should eventually complete (second waits for channel space)
    let timeout = Duration::from_secs(5);
```

```
}
        }
    }

    fn emit(&self, event: SupervisorEvent) {
        let _ = self.event_tx.send(event);
    }

    async fn handle_command(&mut self, cmd: SupervisorCommand) -> Result<(), SupervisorError> {
        match cmd {
            SupervisorCommand::StartChild { spec, reply } => {
                let result = self.do_start_child(spec).await;
                let _ = reply.send(result);
            }
            SupervisorCommand::StopChild { name, reply } => {
                let result = self.do_stop_child(&name).await;
                let _ = reply.send(result);
            }
            SupervisorCommand::GetChild { name, reply } => {
                let handle = self.children.get(&name).map(|child| {
                    AgentHandle::new(
                        child.id,
                        child.mailbox.clone(),
                        child.logical_cancel.clone(),
                    )
                });
                let _ = reply.send(handle);
            }
            SupervisorCommand::Shutdown => {
                self.drain_all().await;
                self.cancel.cancel();
            }
        }
        Ok(())
    }

    async fn do_start_child(&mut self, spec: ChildSpec) -> Result<AgentHandle, SupervisorError> {
        let name = spec.name.clone();
        let id = AgentId::new();
        let logical_cancel = CancellationToken::new();
        let child_cancel = logical_cancel.child_token();

        // Create stable mailbox with dummy sender
        let (dummy_tx, _) = mpsc::channel(1);
        let mailbox = Arc::new(MailboxSlot::new(dummy_tx));

        // Build peers map from existing alive children
        let peers: HashMap<String, AgentHandle> = self
            .children
            .iter()
            .filter(|(_, c)| c.alive)
            .map(|(n, c)| {
                (
                    n.clone(),
                    AgentHandle::new(c.id, c.mailbox.clone(), c.logical_cancel.clone()),
                )
            })
            .collect();

        // Register agent budget slot if budget tracking is active
        if let Some(ref budget) = self.budget {
            budget.register_agent(&name, spec.token_budget);
        }

        // Call factory
        let ctx = ChildContext {
            id,
            generation: 0,
            cancel: child_cancel.clone(),
            peers,
            llm: None,
            budget: self.budget.clone(),
            tools: ToolRegistry::new(),
        };
        let spawned = (spec.factory)(ctx)
            .await
            .map_err(|e| SupervisorError::SpawnFailed(e.to_string()))?;

        // Swap real sender into stable mailbox
        mailbox.swap(spawned.sender);

        // Build the stable handle
        let handle = AgentHandle::new(id, mailbox.clone(), logical_cancel.clone());

        // Spawn future in JoinSet
        let abort = self.join_set.spawn(spawned.future);
        let task_id = abort.id();
        self.task_map.insert(task_id, name.clone());

        let tracker = RestartTracker::new(&spec.config.restart_policy);

        let state = ChildState {
            spec,
            id,
            generation: 0,
            progress: Some(spawned.progress),
            child_cancel: Some(child_cancel),
            mailbox,
            logical_cancel,
            tracker,
            alive: true,
            hung: false,
        };

        self.children.insert(name.clone(), state);
        self.child_order.push(name.clone());

        self.emit(SupervisorEvent::ChildStarted {
            name,
            generation: 0,
        });

        Ok(handle)
    }

    async fn do_stop_child(&mut self, name: &str) -> Result<(), SupervisorError> {
        let child = self
            .children
            .get_mut(name)
            .ok_or_else(|| SupervisorError::ChildNotFound(name.into()))?;

        if let Some(cancel) = child.child_cancel.take() {
            cancel.cancel();
        }
        child.alive = false;
        Ok(())
    }

    async fn handle_child_exit(
        &mut self,
        result: Result<(tokio::task::Id, ChildExit), tokio::task::JoinError>,
    ) -> Result<(), SupervisorError> {
        let (task_id, exit) = match result {
            Ok((id, exit)) => (id, exit),
            Err(e) => {
                let id = e.id();
                (id, ChildExit::Failed(format!("task panicked: {e}")))
            }
        };

        let Some(name) = self.task_map.remove(&task_id) else {
            return Ok(());
        };

        let (old_gen, should_restart) = {
            let Some(child) = self.children.get_mut(&name) else {
                return Ok(());
            };

            let old_gen = child.generation;

```
child.alive = false;
            child.child_cancel = None;
            child.progress = None;

            // Hung children exit with Shutdown, which isn't a "failure" —
            // override so Transient restart policy still kicks in.
            let is_failure = if child.hung {
                child.hung = false;
                true
            } else {
                exit.is_failure()
            };
            let should_restart = child.spec.restart.should_restart(is_failure);
            (old_gen, should_restart)
        };

        let _ = self.event_tx.send(SupervisorEvent::ChildExited {
            name: name.clone(),
            generation: old_gen,
            exit,
        });

        if !should_restart || self.cancel.is_cancelled() {
            return Ok(());
        }

        match self.config.strategy {
            Strategy::OneForOne => {
                // Record in per-child tracker
                let now = tokio::time::Instant::now();
                let child = self.children.get_mut(&name).unwrap();
                child.tracker.record(now);

                if child.tracker.exceeded() {
                    let restarts = child.tracker.total_restarts;
                    let _ = self
                        .event_tx
                        .send(SupervisorEvent::ChildRestartLimitExceeded { name, restarts });
                    return Ok(());
                }

                // Record in per-supervisor intensity tracker
                self.intensity.record(now);
                if self.intensity.exceeded() {
                    let total_restarts = self.intensity.total_restarts;
                    let _ = self
                        .event_tx
                        .send(SupervisorEvent::RestartIntensityExceeded { total_restarts });
                    self.drain_all().await;
                    return Err(SupervisorError::RestartIntensityExceeded { total_restarts });
                }

                // Compute backoff delay and sleep
                let child = self.children.get(&name).unwrap();
                let delay = child.tracker.backoff_delay();
                tokio::time::sleep(delay).await;

                // Don't restart if cancelled during backoff sleep
                if self.cancel.is_cancelled() {
                    return Ok(());
                }

                // Build peers map from alive siblings
                let peers: HashMap<String, AgentHandle> = self
                    .children
                    .iter()
                    .filter(|(n, c)| c.alive && *n != &name)
                    .map(|(n, c)| {
                        (
                            n.clone(),
                            AgentHandle::new(c.id, c.mailbox.clone(), c.logical_cancel.clone()),
                        )
                    })
                    .collect();

                let child = self.children.get_mut(&name).unwrap();

                // Increment generation and create new per-generation cancel token
                let new_gen = old_gen + 1;
                let child_cancel = child.logical_cancel.child_token();

                let ctx = ChildContext {
                    id: child.id,
                    generation: new_gen,
                    cancel: child_cancel.clone(),
                    peers,
                    llm: None,
                    budget: self.budget.clone(),
                    tools: ToolRegistry::new(),
                };

                let spawned = match (child.spec.factory)(ctx).await {
                    Ok(s) => s,
                    Err(_) => {
                        // Factory failed — leave child dead
                        return Ok(());
                    }
                };

                // Hot-swap sender into stable mailbox
                child.mailbox.swap(spawned.sender);

                // Spawn new future in JoinSet
                let abort = self.join_set.spawn(spawned.future);
                let new_task_id = abort.id();
                self.task_map.insert(new_task_id, name.clone());

                // Update child state
                child.generation = new_gen;
                child.progress = Some(spawned.progress);
                child.child_cancel = Some(child_cancel);
                child.alive = true;

                let _ = self.event_tx.send(SupervisorEvent::ChildRestarted {
                    name,
                    old_gen,
                    new_gen,
                    delay,
                });
            }
            Strategy::OneForAll => {
                self.restart_all(&name).await?;
            }
        }

        Ok(())
    }

    async fn restart_all(&mut self, trigger_name: &str) -> Result<(), SupervisorError> {
        // 1. Cancel all alive children (except the one that already exited)
        for (name, child) in &self.children {
            if name != trigger_name
                && let Some(ref cancel) = child.child_cancel
            {
                cancel.cancel();
            }
        }

        // 2. Wait for all to exit
        while self.join_set.join_next().await.is_some() {}
        self.task_map.clear();

        // 3. Record restart in per-supervisor intensity tracker
        let now = tokio::time::Instant::now();
        self.intensity.record(now);
        if self.intensity.exceeded() {
            let total = self.intensity.total_restarts;
            let _ = self
                .event_tx
                .send(SupervisorEvent::RestartIntensityExceeded {

```
//! Private indirection layer for hot-swapping agent mailboxes on restart.

use std::sync::Arc;

use arc_swap::ArcSwap;
use tokio::sync::mpsc;

use super::message::AgentMessage;
use crate::error::AgentError;

/// Wraps an `mpsc::Sender` behind `ArcSwap` for lock-free hot-swapping.
pub(crate) struct MailboxSlot {
    sender: ArcSwap<mpsc::Sender<AgentMessage>>,
}

impl MailboxSlot {
    pub(crate) fn new(sender: mpsc::Sender<AgentMessage>) -> Self {
        Self {
            sender: ArcSwap::from_pointee(sender),
        }
    }

    /// Atomically replaces the inner sender.
    pub(crate) fn swap(&self, new_sender: mpsc::Sender<AgentMessage>) {
        self.sender.store(Arc::new(new_sender));
    }

    /// Sends a message with one retry on closed channel (restart race).
    pub(crate) async fn send(&self, msg: AgentMessage) -> Result<(), AgentError> {
        let sender = self.sender.load_full();
        match sender.send(msg).await {
            Ok(()) => Ok(()),
            Err(mpsc::error::SendError(msg)) => {
                let sender = self.sender.load_full();
                sender.send(msg).await.map_err(|_| AgentError::Unavailable)
            }
        }
    }
}
```

```
use std::time::Duration;

#[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy)]
pub enum Strategy {
    OneForOne,
    OneForAll,
}

#[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy, Default)]
pub enum ChildRestart {
    Permanent,
    #[default]
    Transient,
    Temporary,
}

impl ChildRestart {
    pub fn should_restart(&self, is_failure: bool) -> bool {
        match self {
            Self::Permanent => true,
            Self::Transient => is_failure,
            Self::Temporary => false,
        }
    }
}

#[derive(Debug, Clone)]
pub struct ShutdownPolicy {
    pub grace: Duration,
}

impl Default for ShutdownPolicy {
    fn default() -> Self {
        Self {
            grace: Duration::from_secs(5),
        }
    }
}

#[derive(Debug, Clone)]
pub struct RestartIntensity {
    pub max_restarts: u32,
    pub window: Duration,
}

impl Default for RestartIntensity {
    fn default() -> Self {
        Self {
            max_restarts: 10,
            window: Duration::from_secs(60),
        }
    }
}

#[derive(Debug, Clone)]
pub struct SupervisorConfig {
    pub strategy: Strategy,
    pub intensity: RestartIntensity,
    pub hang_check_interval: Duration,
    pub event_capacity: usize,
}

impl Default for SupervisorConfig {
    fn default() -> Self {
        Self {
            strategy: Strategy::OneForOne,
            intensity: RestartIntensity::default(),
            hang_check_interval: Duration::from_secs(1),
            event_capacity: 64,
        }
    }
}
```

/// Mock LLM that returns a fixed number of tokens per call.

impl LlmProvider for MockLlm {
    fn chat<'a>(
        &'a self,
        _req: &'a LlmRequest,
    ) -> Pin<Box<dyn Future<Output = Result<LlmResponse, mra::error::LlmError>> + Send + 'a>> {
        let tokens = self.0;
        Box::pin(async move {
            Ok(LlmResponse {
                content: "mock".into(),
                prompt_tokens: tokens / 2,
                completion_tokens: tokens - tokens / 2,
                tool_calls: vec![],

        })

                role: Role::User,
                content: input.instruction.clone(),

                tool_call_id: None,
            }],
            temperature: None,
            max_tokens: None,
            tools: None,
        };
        let response = ctx.chat(&request).await?;
        let tokens = response.total_tokens();
        Ok(AgentReply {
            task_id: input.id,
            output: response.content,
            self_tokens: tokens,
            total_tokens: tokens,
        })
    }
}

                new_gen,
                delay: Duration::from_millis(0),
            });

    async fn drain_all(&mut self) {
        self.emit(SupervisorEvent::SupervisorStopping);
        for child in self.children.values() {
            if let Some(ref cancel) = child.child_cancel {
                cancel.cancel();
            }
        }
        while self.join_set.join_next().await.is_some() {}
    }

use serde::{Deserialize, Serialize};
use tokio::sync::oneshot;

use crate::error::AgentError;
use crate::ids::TaskId;

/// A unit of work submitted to an agent.
///
/// Contains a unique [`TaskId`] for correlation, a human-readable
/// instruction, and an optional JSON context blob for structured input.
#[derive(Debug, Serialize, Deserialize)]
pub struct Task {
    pub id: TaskId,
    pub instruction: String,
    pub context: serde_json::Value,
}

impl Task {
    /// Creates a new task with a generated [`TaskId`] and null context.
    pub fn new(instruction: impl Into<String>) -> Self {
        Self {
            id: TaskId::new(),
            instruction: instruction.into(),
            context: serde_json::Value::Null,
        }
    }
}

/// The result produced by an agent after processing a [`Task`].
#[derive(Debug, Serialize, Deserialize)]
pub struct AgentReply {
    /// The id of the [`Task`] this reply corresponds to.
    pub task_id: TaskId,
    /// The agent's output text.
    pub output: String,
    /// This agent's direct LLM token usage (not including nested agents).
    pub self_tokens: u64,
    /// End-to-end pipeline total (self + nested agents). Telemetry only.
    pub total_tokens: u64,
}

/// Internal message envelope sent through the agent's bounded `mpsc` channel.
pub(crate) enum AgentMessage {
    Execute {
        task: Task,
        respond_to: oneshot::Sender<Result<AgentReply, AgentError>>,
    },
    /// Initiate graceful shutdown. The runner closes the receiver, drains
    /// buffered work until `deadline`, then fails any remaining callers
    /// with [`AgentError::Cancelled`].
    Shutdown { deadline: tokio::time::Instant },
}
```

use mra::budget::BudgetTracker;

#[test]
fn test_charge_under_limit() {
    let tracker = BudgetTracker::builder()
        .global_limit(1000)
        .build_unconnected();

    assert!(tracker.charge_global(500).is_ok());
    let usage = tracker.run_usage();
    assert_eq!(usage.used, 500);
    assert_eq!(usage.limit, Some(1000));
}

#[test]
fn test_charge_exceeds_global_limit() {
    let tracker = BudgetTracker::builder()
        .global_limit(100)
        .build_unconnected();

    assert!(tracker.charge_global(60).is_ok());
    let result = tracker.charge_global(60);
    assert!(result.is_err());
}

#[test]
fn test_no_limit_means_unlimited() {
    let tracker = BudgetTracker::builder().build_unconnected();

    assert!(tracker.charge_global(999_999).is_ok());
    let usage = tracker.run_usage();
    assert_eq!(usage.used, 999_999);
    assert_eq!(usage.limit, None);
}

#[test]
fn test_multiple_charges_accumulate() {
    let tracker = BudgetTracker::builder()
        .global_limit(1000)
        .build_unconnected();

    tracker.charge_global(200).unwrap();
    tracker.charge_global(300).unwrap();
    assert_eq!(tracker.run_usage().used, 500);
}

// Per-agent tests

#[test]
fn test_per_agent_charge_under_limit() {
    let tracker = BudgetTracker::builder()
        .global_limit(10_000)
        .build_unconnected();

    tracker.register_agent("writer", Some(500));
    assert!(tracker.charge("writer", 200).is_ok());

    let usage = tracker.agent_usage("writer").unwrap();
    assert_eq!(usage.used, 200);
    assert_eq!(usage.limit, Some(500));
}

#[test]
fn test_per_agent_exceeds_own_limit() {
    let tracker = BudgetTracker::builder()
        .global_limit(10_000)
        .build_unconnected();

    tracker.register_agent("writer", Some(100));
    assert!(tracker.charge("writer", 60).is_ok());
    let result = tracker.charge("writer", 60);
    assert!(result.is_err());
}

#[test]
fn test_per_agent_also_charges_global() {
    let tracker = BudgetTracker::builder()
        .global_limit(10_000)
        .build_unconnected();

    tracker.register_agent("writer", Some(5000));
    tracker.charge("writer", 300).unwrap();

    assert_eq!(tracker.run_usage().used, 300);
    assert_eq!(tracker.agent_usage("writer").unwrap().used, 300);
}

#[test]
fn test_global_exceeded_via_per_agent_charges() {
    let tracker = BudgetTracker::builder()
        .global_limit(100)
        .build_unconnected();

    tracker.register_agent("a", None);
    tracker.register_agent("b", None);

    tracker.charge("a", 60).unwrap();
    let result = tracker.charge("b", 60);
    assert!(result.is_err());

    // Both counters should reflect actual spend even when global trips
    assert_eq!(tracker.agent_usage("b").unwrap().used, 60);
    assert_eq!(tracker.run_usage().used, 120);
}

fn test_agent_no_limit_unlimited() {
    let tracker = BudgetTracker::builder().build_unconnected();

    tracker.register_agent("writer", None);
    assert!(tracker.charge("writer", 999_999).is_ok());
    assert_eq!(tracker.agent_usage("writer").unwrap().used, 999_999);
}

    assert!(tracker.agent_usage("ghost").is_none());
}

```
}

        Ok(())
    }

    async fn drain_all(&mut self) {
        self.emit(SupervisorEvent::SupervisorStopping);
        for child in self.children.values() {
            if let Some(ref cancel) = child.child_cancel {
                cancel.cancel();
            }
        }
        while self.join_set.join_next().await.is_some() {}
    }

    async fn check_hangs(&mut self) {
        let mut hangs = Vec::new();

        for (name, child) in &self.children {
            if !child.alive {
                continue;
            }
            let Some(hang_timeout) = child.spec.hang_timeout else {
                continue;
            };
            let Some(ref progress_rx) = child.progress else {
                continue;
            };

            let progress = progress_rx.borrow();
            if progress.busy && progress.last_progress.elapsed() > hang_timeout {
                let elapsed = progress.last_progress.elapsed();
                hangs.push((name.clone(), child.generation, elapsed));
            }
        }

        for (name, generation, elapsed) in hangs {
            let _ = self.event_tx.send(SupervisorEvent::HangDetected {
                name: name.clone(),
                generation,
                elapsed,
            });

            if let Some(child) = self.children.get_mut(&name)
                && let Some(cancel) = child.child_cancel.take()
            {
                child.hung = true;
                cancel.cancel();
            }
        }

```
use std::time::Duration;

use super::ChildExit;

/// Lifecycle events emitted by the supervisor via a `broadcast` channel.
///
/// Subscribe with [`SupervisorHandle::subscribe`](super::SupervisorHandle::subscribe)
/// to observe starts, stops, restarts, and hang detections.
#[derive(Debug, Clone)]
pub enum SupervisorEvent {
    /// The supervisor's event loop has started.
    SupervisorStarted,
    /// The supervisor is draining children before shutting down.
    SupervisorStopping,
    /// A child was spawned (or respawned) successfully.
    ChildStarted { name: String, generation: u64 },
    /// A child's run future completed.
    ChildExited {
        name: String,
        generation: u64,
        exit: ChildExit,
    },
    /// A child was restarted after a failure, with the backoff `delay` applied.
    ChildRestarted {
        name: String,
        old_gen: u64,
        new_gen: u64,
        delay: Duration,
    },
    /// A child has been busy without reporting progress longer than its timeout.
    HangDetected {
        name: String,
        generation: u64,
        elapsed: Duration,
    },
    /// A single child hit its per-child restart limit and will not be restarted again.
    ChildRestartLimitExceeded { name: String, restarts: u64 },
    /// Supervisor-wide restart intensity exceeded — the supervisor shuts down.
    RestartIntensityExceeded { total_restarts: u64 },
    /// A token budget was exceeded (reserved for future event-emitter wiring).
    BudgetExceeded { name: String, used: u64, limit: u64 },
}
```

```
//! Swarm runtime — thin wrapper around the root supervisor.

use std::sync::Arc;

use tokio::sync::broadcast;
use tokio::task::JoinHandle;

use crate::agent::AgentHandle;
use crate::budget::{AgentUsage, BudgetTracker, RunUsage};
use crate::error::SupervisorError;
use crate::supervisor::{ChildSpec, SupervisorConfig, SupervisorEvent, SupervisorHandle};

/// Manages a supervised set of agents.
///
/// Thin wrapper around a root [`SupervisorHandle`]. Agents are spawned
/// via [`ChildSpec`] factories and managed by the supervisor's restart
/// and hang-detection policies.
pub struct SwarmRuntime {
    supervisor: SupervisorHandle,
    join: JoinHandle<Result<(), SupervisorError>>,
    budget: Option<Arc<BudgetTracker>>,
}

impl SwarmRuntime {
    /// Creates a new runtime backed by a supervisor with the given config.
    pub fn new(config: SupervisorConfig) -> Self {
        let (supervisor, join) = SupervisorHandle::start(config);
        Self {
            supervisor,
            join,
            budget: None,
        }
    }

    /// Creates a new runtime with a global token budget.
    ///
    /// When the budget is exceeded, agents receive
    /// `AgentError::BudgetExceeded` from
    /// [`AgentCtx::chat`](crate::agent::AgentCtx::chat).
    pub fn with_budget(config: SupervisorConfig, global_limit: u64) -> Self {
        let budget = Arc::new(
            BudgetTracker::builder()
                .global_limit(global_limit)
                .build_unconnected(),
        );
        let (supervisor, join) = SupervisorHandle::start_with_budget(config, Some(budget.clone()));
        Self {
            supervisor,
            join,
            budget: Some(budget),
        }
    }

    /// Spawns a child agent via the supervisor.
    pub async fn spawn(&self, spec: ChildSpec) -> Result<AgentHandle, SupervisorError> {
        self.supervisor.start_child(spec).await
    }

    /// Looks up a child handle by name.
    pub async fn get_handle_by_name(&self, name: &str) -> Option<AgentHandle> {
        self.supervisor.child(name).await
    }

    /// Subscribes to supervisor events.
    pub fn subscribe(&self) -> broadcast::Receiver<SupervisorEvent> {
        self.supervisor.subscribe()
    }

    /// Returns current global token usage, if a budget is configured.
    pub fn token_usage(&self) -> Option<RunUsage> {
        self.budget.clone().map(|b| b.run_usage())
    }

    /// Returns per-agent token usage, if a budget is configured.
    pub fn agent_token_usage(&self, name: &str) -> Option<AgentUsage> {
        match self.budget.clone() {
            Some(b) => b.agent_usage(name),
            None => None,
        }
    }

    /// Gracefully shuts down all agents and the supervisor.
    pub async fn shutdown(self) {
        self.supervisor.shutdown().await;
        let _ = self.join.await;
    }
}
```

```
//! Shell command tool -- runs a command via `/bin/sh -c` with a
//! configurable timeout, output truncation (32 KB), and `kill_on_drop`.

use std::future::Future;
use std::pin::Pin;
use std::process::Stdio;
use std::time::Duration;

use schemars::JsonSchema;
use serde::Deserialize;
use serde_json::Value;

use crate::error::ToolError;

use super::{Tool, ToolOutput, ToolSpec};

#[derive(Deserialize, JsonSchema)]
#[serde(deny_unknown_fields)]
struct ShellArgs {
    /// The shell command to execute
    command: String,
}

const MAX_OUTPUT_BYTES: usize = 32_768;

fn truncate(s: &str) -> String {
    if s.len() <= MAX_OUTPUT_BYTES {
        s.to_string()
    } else {
        let mut end = MAX_OUTPUT_BYTES;
        while end > 0 && !s.is_char_boundary(end) {
            end -= 1;
        }
        let mut out = s[..end].to_string();
        out.push_str("\n...[truncated]");
        out
    }
}

/// Runs shell commands on the host. The child process is killed if
/// the timeout expires or the future is dropped.
///
/// Output (stdout on success, stderr on failure) is capped at 32 KB
/// with UTF-8-safe truncation.
pub struct ShellTool {
    spec: ToolSpec,
    timeout: Duration,
}

impl Default for ShellTool {
```

+use std::collections::HashMap;
+use std::sync::Arc;
+
+use tokio_util::sync::CancellationToken;
+
+use crate::budget::BudgetTracker;
+use crate::config::AgentConfig;
+use crate::ids::AgentId;
+use crate::llm::LlmProvider;
+use crate::supervisor::child::{ChildContext, SpawnedChild};
+use crate::tool::ToolRegistry;
+
+use super::AgentBehavior;
+use super::handle::AgentHandle;
+use super::runner::SpawnedAgent;
+
+/// Builder for spawning agents with sensible defaults.
+///
+/// Only a name and behavior are required — everything else defaults
+/// to empty/None. Use optional setters to override.
+///
+/// Two terminal methods:
+/// - [`.spawn()`](Self::spawn) — standalone Tokio task
+/// - [`.spawn_child()`](Self::spawn_child) — unspawned future for supervisor
+#[must_use]
+pub struct AgentSpawn<B> {
+    id: AgentId,
+    config: AgentConfig,
+    behavior: B,
+    peers: HashMap<String, AgentHandle>,
+    llm: Option<Arc<dyn LlmProvider>>,
+    cancel: CancellationToken,
+    budget: Option<Arc<BudgetTracker>>,
+    tools: ToolRegistry,
+}
+
+impl<B: AgentBehavior> AgentSpawn<B> {
+    /// Creates a builder with a name and behavior.
+    ///
+    /// Defaults: fresh `AgentId`, `AgentConfig::new(name)`, no peers,
+    /// no LLM, fresh `CancellationToken`, no budget, empty tools.
+    pub fn new(name: impl Into<String>, behavior: B) -> Self {
+        let name = name.into();
+        Self::from_config(AgentConfig::new(&name), behavior)
+    }
+
+    /// Creates a builder with a pre-built config and behavior.
+    ///
+    /// Use when you need to customize `AgentConfig` fields like
+    /// `mailbox_size` or `restart_policy` beyond the defaults.
+    pub fn from_config(config: AgentConfig, behavior: B) -> Self {
+        Self {
+            id: AgentId::new(),
+            config,
+            behavior,
+            peers: HashMap::new(),
+            llm: None,
+            cancel: CancellationToken::new(),
+            budget: None,
+            tools: ToolRegistry::new(),
+        }
+    }
+
+    /// Applies all fields from a [`ChildContext`], overriding id,
+    /// cancel, peers, llm, budget, and tools.
+    ///
+    /// Used internally by [`ChildSpec::from_behavior`](crate::supervisor::ChildSpec::from_behavior).
+    pub(crate) fn with_child_ctx(mut self, ctx: ChildContext) -> Self {
+        self.id = ctx.id;
+        self.cancel = ctx.cancel;
+        self.peers = ctx.peers;
+        self.llm = ctx.llm;
+        self.budget = ctx.budget;
+        self.tools = ctx.tools;
+        self
+    }
+
+    /// Overrides the agent's unique identifier.
+    pub fn id(mut self, id: AgentId) -> Self {
+        self.id = id;
+        self
+    }
+
+    /// Injects named peer handles for inter-agent delegation.
+    pub fn peers(mut self, peers: HashMap<String, AgentHandle>) -> Self {
+        self.peers = peers;
+        self
+    }
+
+    /// Sets the shared LLM provider.
+    pub fn llm(mut self, llm: Arc<dyn LlmProvider>) -> Self {
+        self.llm = Some(llm);
+        self
+    }
```

### Tool Call [completed]: 

**Timestamp:** 2026-03-28 17:54:45

```
#+TITLE: mra
#+OPTIONS: toc:2 num:nil

#+begin_quote
*WIP.* Don't depend on this yet.
#+end_quote

You know you can just make things right, and i just want something lightweight and make me happy. So here we go, a multi-agent runtime for Rust. Spawn AI agents as lightweight Tokio actors, wire them together, and let them talk to LLMs

* What?

Each agent runs as its own async task with a bounded =mpsc= mailbox. Agents talk to each other through handles, call LLMs, and get restarted by a supervisor if they crash or stop responding. No shared mutable state.

If you've used Erlang/OTP, this is that idea applied to LLM pipelines, in Rust.

* Quick look

Spawn an agent in two lines:

#+begin_src rust
use mra::agent::{AgentSpawn, Task};

let spawned = AgentSpawn::new("writer", Writer).llm(llm).spawn();
let reply = spawned.handle.execute(Task::new("write something")).await?;
#+end_src

=AgentSpawn= is a typed builder. Only a name and behavior are required -- everything else (LLM, tools, budget, peers) defaults to empty/None. Chain setters for what you need, then call =.spawn()= for a standalone task or =.spawn_child()= for supervisor-managed agents.

Here's a behavior that calls an LLM and delegates to a peer:

#+begin_src rust
struct Writer;

impl AgentBehavior for Writer {
    async fn handle(
        &mut self,
        ctx: &mut AgentCtx,
        input: Task,
    ) -> Result<AgentReply, AgentError> {
        let response = ctx.chat(&LlmRequest {
            model: None,
            messages: vec![
                ChatMessage { role: Role::System, content: "You are a writer.".into(), tool_calls: vec![], tool_call_id: None },
                ChatMessage { role: Role::User, content: input.instruction, tool_calls: vec![], tool_call_id: None },
            ],
            temperature: Some(0.7),
            max_tokens: Some(2048),
            tools: None,
        }).await?;

        // The supervisor injects peer handles automatically
        let editor = ctx.peers.get("editor").expect("editor peer");
        let reply = editor.execute(Task::new(response.content)).await?;

        Ok(AgentReply {
            task_id: input.id,
            output: reply.output,
            self_tokens: response.total_tokens(),
            total_tokens: response.total_tokens() + reply.total_tokens,
        })
    }
}
#+end_src

* Supervision

The supervisor sits in a =select!= loop watching for three things: child exits, incoming commands, and hang-check ticks. When something goes wrong, it decides what to do based on the restart policy.

Restart strategies:
- =OneForOne= -- restart the crashed agent only
- =OneForAll= -- restart every agent when one crashes

Restart policies per child:
- =Permanent= -- always restart, regardless of how it exited
- =Transient= -- restart only on failure (not normal exit)
- =Temporary= -- never restart

Other stuff the supervisor handles:
- Exponential backoff between restarts (configurable base and cap)
- A global restart intensity limit -- too many restarts in a window and it gives up
- Hang detection by polling each agent's last-activity timestamp
- Peer injection -- agents get handles to their siblings through =ctx.peers=
- Hot-swap mailbox via =ArcSwap= -- when an agent restarts, existing handles keep working because the supervisor swaps the new channel sender into the same stable slot

#+begin_src rust
use mra::config::AgentConfig;
use mra::runtime::SwarmRuntime;
use mra::supervisor::{ChildSpec, ChildRestart, SupervisorConfig};

let runtime = SwarmRuntime::new(SupervisorConfig::default());

// ChildSpec::from_behavior handles all the factory boilerplate.
// Just give it a config and a closure that returns a behavior.
let editor_spec = ChildSpec::from_behavior(AgentConfig::new("editor"), |_| Editor)
    .with_restart(ChildRestart::Permanent);

// Spawn in dependency order. The supervisor populates ctx.peers
// with whatever siblings are already alive.
runtime.spawn(editor_spec).await?;
runtime.spawn(ChildSpec::from_behavior(AgentConfig::new("writer"), |_| Writer)).await?;
```

Excellent! Now I have enough information to provide a comprehensive architecture analysis. Let me create the detailed report:

## Comprehensive Architecture Analysis: mra (Multi-agent Runtime Architecture)

Based on thorough exploration of the Rust multi-agent runtime codebase, here's a detailed analysis of the architecture, friction points, and areas for improvement.

### 1. OVERALL DIRECTORY STRUCTURE AND MODULE ORGANIZATION

**Core Modules (830 lines agent + 1,196 lines supervisor):**

- **`agent/`** (830 total lines across 7 files):
  - `mod.rs` (56) - Public trait and re-exports
  - `handle.rs` (76) - Cloneable agent handle with mailbox slot reference
  - `ctx.rs` (199) - Runtime context with LLM/tool/budget/peer access
  - `runner.rs` (246) - The async actor loop and task lifecycle
  - `spawn.rs` (162) - Typed builder for agent construction
  - `mailbox.rs` (39) - Lock-free hot-swappable channel wrapper
  - `message.rs` (52) - Internal message types

- **`supervisor/`** (1,196 lines across 7 files):
  - `runner.rs` (531) - Main supervisor event loop and restart logic
  - `child.rs` (197) - Child spec, context, and factory patterns
  - `config.rs` (72) - Restart/intensity policies
  - `tracker.rs` (206) - Restart timing and exponential backoff
  - `handle.rs` (116) - SupervisorHandle for command dispatch
  - `event.rs` (42) - Event types for lifecycle observation
  - `mod.rs` (32) - Re-exports

- **`tool/`** (3.8k lines):
  - Native shell, file-read, file-edit implementations
  - Extensible `Tool` trait with `Pin<Box<dyn Future>>` dispatch
  - `ToolRegistry` for name-based lookup

- **`llm/`** (~2.5k lines):
  - `LlmProvider` trait with boxed futures for dynamic dispatch
  - OpenRouter client implementation
  - Chat message and response types

- **Supporting modules**:
  - `budget.rs` - Lock-free atomic token budgeting (global + per-agent)
  - `config.rs` - Agent/runtime configuration with builder patterns
  - `error.rs` - Comprehensive error types with classification for retry decisions
  - `ids.rs` - Unique identifiers for agents and tasks
  - `runtime.rs` - Thin wrapper around supervisor + budget

**Test Coverage: 130+ tests across 10 files (2,538 lines)**
- Heaviest coverage in `tool.rs` (673 lines) and `supervisor.rs` (524 lines)
- Lighter coverage for LLM (234), spawn_builder (239), agent (259), budget_integration (174)

---

### 2. KEY ABSTRACTIONS AND RELATIONSHIPS

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│ User Code: Implement AgentBehavior trait                    │
│ async fn handle(&mut self, ctx: &mut AgentCtx, task: Task)  │
└────────────────────┬────────────────────────────────────────┘
                     │
        ┌────────────▼──────────────┐
        │ AgentSpawn<B> Builder      │ (typed, monomorphic)
        │ - name, config             │
        │ - behavior, peers          │
        │ - llm, budget, tools       │
        │ - cancel token             │
        └────────────┬───────────────┘
              ┌──────┴──────┐
              │             │
        ┌─────▼────┐   ┌───▼────────┐
        │.spawn()  │   │.spawn_child()
        │          │   │
        ▼          ▼   ▼
   ┌─────────────────────────────┐
   │ AgentRunner<B>              │ (monomorphic dispatch)
   │ - receiver: mpsc            │
   │ - ctx: AgentCtx             │
   │ - behavior: B               │
   │ - select! loop              │
   └────────────┬────────────────┘
                │
        ┌───────▼────────┐
        │ SpawnedAgent   │
        │ ┌────────────┐ │
        │ │ handle     │ │────────────────┐
        │ │ progress   │ │                │
        │ │ join       │ │                │
        │ └────────────┘ │                │
        └────────────────┘                │
                                          ▼
                            ┌─────────────────────────┐
                            │ AgentHandle (cloneable) │
                            │ ┌────────────────────┐ │
                            │ │ mailbox: MailboxSlot
                            │ │ (ArcSwap wrapper)  │ │
                            │ │ cancel: Token      │ │
                            │ └────────────────────┘ │
                            └────────┬────────────────┘
                                     │
                    ┌────────────────┼────────────────┐
                    │                │                │
                    ▼                ▼                ▼
            ┌──────────────┐  ┌─────────┐  ┌──────────────┐
            │   Peers Map  │  │ execute()│  │   Shutdown   │
            │ (delegation) │  │  (send)  │  │  Cancellation│
            └──────────────┘  └─────────┘  └──────────────┘
```

**ChildSpec Factory Pattern:**
```
ChildSpec::from_behavior(config, |ctx| Behavior)
    ↓
ChildFactory (boxed async Fn(ChildContext) → Result<SpawnedChild, Error>)
    ↓
SupervisorRunner.do_start_child()
    ├─ creates ChildContext (id, gen, cancel token, peers, llm, budget, tools)
    ├─ calls factory(ctx)
    └─ hot-swaps sender into stable MailboxSlot
```

**Supervisor Lifecycle:**
```
SupervisorRunner.run() select! loop:
  ├─ join_set.join_next() → handle_child_exit()
  │   ├─ Check restart policy (Permanent/Transient/Temporary)
  │   ├─ Record restart timestamp
  │   ├─ Sleep exponential backoff
  │   ├─ Call factory again with new generation
  │   └─ Hot-swap new sender into stable mailbox
  │
  ├─ command_rx.recv() → handle_command()
  │   ├─ StartChild → do_start_child()
  │   ├─ StopChild → cancel child token
  │   ├─ GetChild → lookup handle
  │   └─ Shutdown → drain_all()
  │
  └─ hang_tick → check_hangs()
      └─ per-child timeout (busy + elapsed > threshold)
         └─ cancel child token + emit event
```

**AgentCtx as Central Hub:**
```
pub struct AgentCtx {
    pub id: AgentId,
    pub name: String,
    pub peers: HashMap<String, AgentHandle>,      // delegation
    pub(crate) llm: Option<Arc<dyn LlmProvider>>, // LLM calls
    pub(crate) budget: Option<Arc<BudgetTracker>>,// token counting
    pub(crate) progress_tx: watch::Sender<...>,   // heartbeats
    pub tools: ToolRegistry,                       // tool invocation
}
```

---

### 3. FRICTION POINTS IN NAVIGATION

#### **High-Friction Areas:**

1. **Supervisor Runner Complexity (531 lines, ~10 async functions)**
   - Single monolithic file handling 6-8 distinct concerns:
     - Child startup (`do_start_child`)
     - Restart logic (per-child tracker + global intensity)
     - Hot-swap mailbox updates
     - Hang detection polling
     - OneForOne vs OneForAll restart cascade
     - Backoff sleep and re-entry race conditions
   - **Friction**: Understanding a restart requires context from 4+ locations:
     - `handle_child_exit()` (lines 228-377) - decides to restart
     - `restart_all()` (lines 378-483) - cascade restart logic (different rules)
     - Backoff computed from `RestartTracker.backoff_delay()` (external)
     - `do_start_child()` (lines 136-214) - duplicated peer/context build logic

2. **MailboxSlot Hot-Swap Abstraction (39 lines, but bridges agent/supervisor)**
   - Uses `ArcSwap` for lock-free hot-swapping
   - Requires understanding:
     - Why a stable slot is needed (restart doesn't invalidate handles)
     - Why retry-on-stale-sender is needed (restart races)
     - ArcSwap memory ordering (Relaxed is sufficient)
   - **Friction**: To understand agent handle lifetime, must bounce through:
     - `AgentHandle.execute()` → `MailboxSlot.send()` → ArcSwap load/store
     - `SupervisorRunner.do_start_child()` → mailbox.swap() → ArcSwap store
   - **Not obvious**: Why `send()` needs two attempts (restart during send race)

3. **ChildFactory Deadlock Warning (but only in docs, not enforced)**
   - `ChildFactory` runs **inside supervisor's event loop**
   - Any `await` on supervisor operations (e.g., `supervisor.start_child()`) deadlocks
   - **Friction**: No type-system enforcement; only documentation guards this
   - **Current state**: Documented in `ChildFactory` and `ChildSpec::new()` doc comments
   - **Risk**: A future developer could add `supervisor.child()` call inside factory closure and not see error until runtime

4. **AgentCtx Public/Private Field Mismatch**
   - `pub id, name, peers, tools` but `pub(crate) llm, budget, progress_tx`
   - **Why?** To enforce budget tracking through `chat()` method
   - **Friction**: Inconsistent API — some fields directly accessible, others gated by methods
   - **Leakage risk**: If someone wants to read `llm` for debugging, no accessor provided

5. **Three-Layer Configuration Patterns**
   - `RestartPolicy` (in `AgentConfig`)
   - `RestartIntensity` (in `SupervisorConfig`)
   - Per-child `token_budget` (in `ChildSpec`)
   - All with similar "backoff base + max + window" semantics
   - **Friction**: Subtle differences in when each applies:
     - Per-child tracker: exponential backoff, checked within restart window
     - Global intensity: linear count in sliding window, no backoff
   - Hard to reason about combined behavior without reading `RestartTracker` and `IntensityTracker` side-by-side

6. **Builder Pattern Duplication: AgentSpawn + ChildSpec**
   - `AgentSpawn::new()` for standalone agents
   - `ChildSpec::from_behavior()` for supervised agents
   - Similar but not identical APIs:
     - `AgentSpawn.with_mailbox_size()` → config builder
     - `ChildSpec.with_restart()`, `with_shutdown_policy()` → different concerns
   - **Friction**: Two paths to create agents, easy to pick wrong one
   - **Current state**: Docs recommend `ChildSpec::from_behavior` as the modern way

---

### 4. SHALLOW MODULES (Interface Complexity ≈ Implementation)

1. **`supervisor/config.rs` (72 lines)**
   - Interface: 5 simple enums/structs with 2-3 fields each
   - Implementation: Pure data with Default impls
   - **Shallow**: No logic; just configuration containers
   - **Fragility**: Changes to restart semantics ripple through `runner.rs`

2. **`supervisor/event.rs` (42 lines)**
   - Interface: `enum SupervisorEvent` with 8 variants
   - Implementation: Just enum definition + doc comments
   - **Shallow**: Event broadcast happens in `runner.rs`, not here

3. **`agent/mailbox.rs` (39 lines)**
   - Interface: `MailboxSlot` with 3 public methods
   - Implementation: ArcSwap wrapper + single retry logic
   - **Shallow**: Core complexity is ArcSwap (external crate)
   - **Fragility**: Retry heuristic (2 attempts on stale sender) is hardcoded; no configuration

4. **`agent/message.rs` (52 lines)**
   - Interface: `enum AgentMessage` and `Task`/`AgentReply` structs
   - Implementation: Pure data types
   - **Shallow**: No behavior; just envelopes

5. **`ids.rs` (12 lines in file)**
   - Simple UUID-style ID generation
   - **Shallow**: Just calls `uuid::Uuid::new_v4()`

---

### 5. TIGHTLY-COUPLED MODULES & INTEGRATION RISK

1. **Agent ↔ Supervisor Coupling (HIGH RISK)**
   - **Forward coupling**: Agent doesn't know about supervisor
   - **Backward coupling**: Supervisor tightly couples to Agent internals:
     - Direct access to `MailboxSlot` (must match sender type)
     - Must recreate `AgentCtx` with identical semantics
     - Must manage cancellation tokens (logical per-gen, physical child)
     - Hardcoded `ArcSwap` retry heuristic in `MailboxSlot.send()`
   - **Risk**: Restarting an agent requires Supervisor to understand:
     - How to rebuild `ChildContext` (generation, peers, cancel)
     - That mailbox swap must happen after factory completes
     - That old senders must be drained before swap
   - **Integration point**: `do_start_child()` lines 136-214 duplicates context-building logic from `AgentSpawn.with_child_ctx()`
     - If `ChildContext` fields change, both places must update
     - No shared constructor to enforce consistency

2. **Budget Tracker ↔ Agent/Supervisor Coupling**
   - **Agent uses**: `AgentCtx.chat()` calls `budget.charge()`
   - **Supervisor uses**: Registers agents on spawn, injects budget into `ChildContext`
   - **Risk**: Agent names are string keys; if agent renames during restart but registration doesn't update, budgets become orphaned
   - **Current code**: `budget.register_agent()` creates if not exists, preserving counters across restarts
     - **Hidden assumption**: Same agent name = same budget slot across generations
     - Fragile if names become dynamic

3. **ToolRegistry ↔ AgentCtx**
   - Registry cloned and injected into every `AgentCtx`
   - **Risk**: Tools are `Arc<dyn Tool>`, so all agents share the same tool instances
   - **Assumption**: Tools are stateless or use interior mutability
   - **Not enforced**: No `Send + Sync` bound on Tool implementations beyond trait
   - Could hide data races if someone stores mutable state in a tool

4. **LlmProvider ↔ Budget Tracking**
   - `AgentCtx.chat()` wraps `llm.chat()` and auto-charges budget
   - **Risk**: If LLM provider internally retries on transient errors, budget is charged per-call, not per-logical-request
   - **Current behavior**: Each `chat()` call charges tokens, even if it's a retry
   - **Not documented**: Whether token usage includes all retries or only final attempt

5. **ChildFactory ↔ Supervisor Event Loop (DEADLOCK RISK)**
   - Factory runs **synchronously** inside supervisor's `run()` loop
   - Any blocking operation inside factory stalls supervisor
   - Any async operation that awaits supervisor command creates deadlock
   - **Enforcement**: Only documented, not type-enforced
   - **Risk level**: HIGH — can silently break during refactor

---

### 6. UNTESTED OR HARD-TO-TEST AREAS

1. **Supervisor Restart Cascades (OneForAll strategy)**
   - **Test coverage**: `supervisor.rs` has tests for OneForOne
   - **Gap**: OneForAll restart (lines 378-483) is implemented but no dedicated test case
   - **Why hard to test**: Requires coordinating multiple children's exit timing
   - **Risk**: Subtle bugs in restart ordering or peer re-injection could go unnoticed

2. **Hang Detection + Restart Interaction**
   - **Test coverage**: `check_hangs()` is called in `run()` loop but hang tests in `supervisor.rs` don't verify that hung children auto-restart
   - **Gap**: No test for "hung → cancelled → restart" cycle
   - **Why hard to test**: Requires timing calibration and coordination with backoff

3. **Budget Integration Edge Cases**
   - `budget_integration.rs` (174 lines) tests basic flows
   - **Gaps**:
     - No test for what happens when budget trips mid-tool-invocation
     - No test for budget exceeded during `chat_with_tools` mid-loop (only one test for this in `tool.rs`)
     - No test for agent restart after budget trip (does counter persist correctly?)
   - **Why hard to test**: Requires mocking LLM to return specific token counts at specific times

4. **Mailbox Hot-Swap Race Conditions**
   - **Test coverage**: None directly
   - **Why hard to test**: ArcSwap requires race conditions to manifest
   - **Risk**: If sender is swapped while task is mid-send, does retry actually reconnect?
   - **Current assumptions**: 
     - `MailboxSlot.send()` retries once on failure (sufficient?)
     - No timeout on retry (could block indefinitely?)

5. **Tool Invocation Error Handling in chat_with_tools**
   - **Test**: `chat_with_tools_tool_error_is_non_fatal` (tool.rs:573)
   - **Gap**: Only tests one tool error; doesn't test:
     - Multiple consecutive tool errors
     - Tool error + budget trip in same iteration
     - Tool error during max-iterations boundary

6. **AgentHandle Backpressure with Bounded Mailbox**
   - **Test**: `test_agent_backpressure` (agent.rs) verifies that multiple senders respect mailbox bound
   - **Gap**: Doesn't test what happens when:
     - Agent crashes while multiple tasks are waiting in queue
     - Mailbox fills up during agent restart
     - Backpressure + cancellation interact

7. **Peer Injection & Delegation Cycles**
   - **Test**: `spawn_with_peers_enables_delegation` verifies delegation works
   - **Gap**: Doesn't test:
     - Circular delegation (A → B → A) causing deadlock
     - Peer name lookups when peer doesn't exist (expects panic)
     - Peer becomes unavailable mid-task

8. **LLM Timeout + Heartbeat Interaction**
   - `AgentCtx.chat()` sends heartbeats every 1 second to prevent hang detection
   - **No test**: Verifies that heartbeats actually prevent supervisor hang-cancel
   - **Gap**: Could timeout in LLM call and still get cancelled by supervisor

---

### 7. PURE FUNCTIONS EXTRACTED FOR TESTABILITY (BUG HIDING RISK)

1. **`RestartTracker::backoff_delay()` (tracker.rs)**
   - **Extracted for testability**: Computes exponential backoff from restart count
   - **Tests**: 3 tests verify the formula (backoff_exponential, backoff_capped_at_max, etc.)
   - **Risk**: Formula is correct in isolation but **how it's called in supervisor.rs matters**:
     ```rust
     let delay = child.tracker.backoff_delay();
     tokio::time::sleep(delay).await;  // in supervisor loop
     ```
     - If supervisor is cancelled during sleep, what happens to restart queue?
     - No test verifies: "cancelled during backoff" scenario
     - Pure function test passes, but integration broken

2. **`LlmResponse::total_tokens()`**
   - **Extracted for testability**: Simple `prompt_tokens + completion_tokens`
   - **Tests**: Implicit in budget tests
   - **Risk**: Assumes LLM provider always sets both fields
     - If provider returns 0 completion tokens, budget logic breaks silently
     - Pure function test would pass (just arithmetic)

3. **`ChildExit::is_failure()` (supervisor/mod.rs)**
   - **Extracted for testability**: Classifies exit as failure
   - **Tests**: 3 simple tests in supervisor.rs
   - **Risk**: Used in restart decision:
     ```rust
     let is_failure = if child.hung { true } else { exit.is_failure() };
     ```
     - "Hung exit" is overridden to force restart even if ChildExit::Shutdown
     - Pure function doesn't know about hung flag override
     - Test of `is_failure()` alone doesn't catch the override logic bug

4. **`MailboxSlot::send()` Retry Logic**
   - **Not a pure function** but deterministic
   - **Tests**: None directly; only tested through agent.rs integration tests
   - **Risk**: Hardcoded "retry once" heuristic
     - What if restart happens between attempts?
     - What if sender closes between load and send?
     - Pure logic test would be good addition

5. **Tracker Timestamp Windowing (tracker.rs)**
   - **Extracted for testability**: `record()` + `exceeded()` + `backoff_delay()`
   - **Tests**: 7 comprehensive tests with mock time
   - **Risk**: Tests use `Instant::now()` which is not mockable in tests
     - Tests work because they use real `tokio::time::Instant`
     - But tests are flaky if CI machine is slow (test timeouts)
   - **Hidden assumption**: Tests assume `Instant::now()` has microsecond precision

---

### 8. ARCHITECTURAL PATTERNS & THEIR STRENGTHS/WEAKNESSES

**Strengths:**
- Monomorphic generic dispatch in agent runner (no dyn, compile-time specialization)
- Lock-free mailbox hot-swap via ArcSwap (enables restarts without handle invalidation)
- Clear separation: AgentBehavior (user impl) vs AgentCtx (runtime API)
- Supervisor as separate event loop with broadcast events (observable)
- Heartbeat-based hang detection (avoids OS thread stalls)
- Error classification (ErrorClass) for intelligent retry decisions
- Budget as shared atomic counters (no locks on critical path)

**Weaknesses:**
- Factory pattern forces async inside supervisor event loop (deadlock hazard)
- Per-child and global restart trackers use similar API but different semantics
- AgentCtx public/private mismatch (some fields gated, others not)
- Supervisor runner is a 531-line monolithic file (hard to understand flow)
- MailboxSlot retry heuristic hardcoded (2 attempts, no timeout)
- Tool registry cloned into every agent (inefficient if many agents/tools)
- Agent names are string keys in budget tracker (fragile if naming changes)

---

### 9. CODE ORGANIZATION IMPROVEMENTS NEEDED

**High Priority:**

1. **Extract supervisor restart logic into separate module**
   - Current: `handle_child_exit()` (150 lines) + `restart_all()` (100 lines) in runner.rs
   - Proposal: New `supervisor/restart.rs` with:
     - `RestartContext` struct (old_gen, new_gen, peers, delay)
     - `restart_single_child(&mut self, name, ctx) -> Result<...>`
     - `restart_all_children(&mut self) -> Result<...>`
   - Benefit: Reduces runner.rs by ~100 lines, easier to reason about restart paths

2. **Unify configuration patterns**
   - Current: RestartPolicy + RestartIntensity have overlapping fields
   - Proposal: New `struct RestartBounds { max: u32, window: Duration }`
   - Benefit: Single source of truth for window-based limiting

3. **Enforce ChildFactory safety**
   - Current: Only documented, no type enforcement
   - Proposal: New `UnsafeChildFactory` wrapper that checks supervisor is not in call stack (via debug assertions)
   - Risk: False sense of security; can't catch all deadlocks
   - Better alternative: Restructure factory to run outside event loop

4. **AgentCtx API consistency**
   - Current: Mix of public and gated fields
   - Proposal: Add `llm_provider()` and `budget_tracker()` accessors
   - Benefit: Symmetry; easier to reason about what's accessible

5. **Extract MailboxSlot retry logic**
   - Current: Hardcoded in `send()` method
   - Proposal: New `struct RetryPolicy { max_attempts: u32, timeout: Option<Duration> }`
   - Benefit: Configurable retry behavior; testable without ArcSwap knowledge

---

### 10. RISK SUMMARY TABLE

| Area | Risk | Friction | Testability | Impact |
|------|------|----------|-------------|--------|
| Supervisor runner | HIGH | HIGH | MEDIUM | Cascading failures in multi-child scenarios |
| ChildFactory deadlock | HIGH | MEDIUM | LOW | Silent hangs during refactoring |
| Mailbox hot-swap | MEDIUM | HIGH | LOW | Agent restart races |
| Budget + agent names | MEDIUM | MEDIUM | LOW | Orphaned budgets on restart |
| Tool + Interior Mut | MEDIUM | LOW | HIGH | Data races if tools store state |
| hang_timeout override | MEDIUM | MEDIUM | MEDIUM | Unexpected restart behavior |
| OneForAll restart | LOW | HIGH | LOW | Untested cascade logic |
| LLM token charging | LOW | MEDIUM | MEDIUM | Retry charging hidden from user |
| Backpressure + cancel | LOW | MEDIUM | MEDIUM | Lost tasks in-flight |
| Peer lookup panic | LOW | LOW | HIGH | Expects agent to handle KeyError |

---

### 11. NAVIGATION FRICTION HOTSPOTS (Where You Get Stuck)

**When you want to understand:**

1. **"How do restarts work?"**
   - Start: `SupervisorEvent::ChildRestarted` (event.rs)
   - Bounce: Look up who emits it → `handle_child_exit()` (runner.rs:260+)
   - Bounce: Depends on `spec.restart.should_restart()` (config.rs)
   - Bounce: If yes, calls `tracker.record()` and `tracker.exceeded()` (tracker.rs)
   - Bounce: Then `backoff_delay()` and `sleep()` (mixed runner/tracker)
   - **Friction**: 4 different files for one concept

2. **"Why doesn't my peer call work?"**
   - Context building happens in 2 places:
     - `SupervisorRunner.do_start_child()` (lines 176-180)
     - `AgentSpawn.with_child_ctx()` (spawn.rs:66)
   - If peer injection is broken, which one is wrong?
   - **Friction**: No single place to understand peer setup

3. **"What happens if budget trips during chat_with_tools?"**
   - Code path: `AgentCtx.chat()` → budget check → charge → error
   - But `chat_with_tools()` calls `chat()` in a loop
   - If one iteration trips budget, do remaining iterations fail?
   - **Friction**: Must read both chat() and chat_with_tools() in sequence

4. **"Why did my agent get hung-cancelled?"**
   - Check: `check_hangs()` (runner.rs:495)
   - Condition: `progress.busy && progress.last_progress.elapsed() > hang_timeout`
   - But who sets `progress.busy` to false?
   - **Friction**: Must trace AgentRunner's progress_tx updates (runner.rs, agent/runner.rs)

---

### SUMMARY

This is a well-structured actor system with clear abstractions, but it has **high friction in cross-module navigation**. The supervisor runner (531 lines) is doing too much, factory pattern creates deadlock risks only guarded by docs, and restart logic is scattered across multiple files with overlapping responsibilities.

The **highest-impact improvements** would be:
1. Extract restart logic into dedicated module
2. Enforce ChildFactory safety at type level (or document + auto-check in tests)
3. Reduce supervisor runner by consolidating restart paths
4. Create shared baseline for restart policies (unify RestartPolicy + RestartIntensity)

agentId: a00d24c (for resuming to continue this agent's work if needed)
```
## Agent (2026-03-28 17:56:13)

## Architecture Improvement Candidates

Based on exploring the codebase, here are the deepening opportunities I found:

| # | Cluster | Why They're Coupled | Dependency Category | Test Impact |
|---|---------|---------------------|---------------------|-------------|
| **1** | **Supervisor Restart Logic** (`runner.rs` lines 228-483, `tracker.rs`, `config.rs`) | `handle_child_exit()` (150 lines) + `restart_all()` (100 lines) scattered across 3 files; restart decision requires bouncing between RestartPolicy, RestartTracker, and IntensityTracker | Internal coordination | Would replace 7+ supervisor tests with boundary tests on a single `RestartManager` |
| **2** | **ChildFactory + Supervisor Event Loop** | Factory runs *inside* supervisor's `select!` loop; deadlock risk only documented, not type-enforced; `do_start_child()` duplicates context-building from `AgentSpawn.with_child_ctx()` | Cross-boundary (async hazard) | Would add compile-time safety; no existing tests catch deadlock |
| **3** | **Agent ↔ Supervisor Context Building** | `ChildContext` constructed in 2 places: `do_start_child()` (runner.rs:176-180) and `AgentSpawn.with_child_ctx()` (spawn.rs:66); if fields change, both must update | Shared ownership of concept | Would consolidate to single `ContextBuilder` with one test suite |
| **4** | **MailboxSlot Hot-Swap + Retry** | 39-line module bridges agent/supervisor; hardcoded 2-attempt retry; ArcSwap semantics leaked to both sides; no direct tests | Internal coordination | Would make retry policy configurable and testable in isolation |
| **5** | **AgentCtx Public/Private API** | `pub id, name, peers, tools` but `pub(crate) llm, budget, progress_tx`; inconsistent gating forces callers to use `chat()` but can directly access other fields | Interface inconsistency | Would unify accessor pattern; cleaner API tests |
| **6** | **Budget Tracker + Agent Names** | String-keyed budget slots; if agent renames during restart, budgets orphan; `register_agent()` creates-if-not-exists hides the coupling | Fragile key coordination | Would make budget identity explicit (AgentId not String) |

## Agent (2026-03-28 17:59:22)

## Problem Space: Supervisor Restart Logic

### The Current State

Restart logic is scattered across **3 files** with **~400 lines** of intertwined code:

```
supervisor/
├── runner.rs    → handle_child_exit() (150 lines), restart_all() (100 lines), do_start_child()
├── tracker.rs   → RestartTracker (per-child backoff), IntensityTracker (global limit)
└── config.rs    → RestartPolicy, RestartIntensity, ChildRestart enums
```

When a child exits, here's the decision flow you have to trace:

```
Child exits
    ↓
handle_child_exit() [runner.rs:228]
    ├─ Was it hung? → force is_failure = true
    ├─ Check ChildRestart policy (Permanent/Transient/Temporary) [config.rs]
    │   └─ should_restart(is_failure) → bool
    ├─ If OneForAll strategy → call restart_all() instead [runner.rs:378]
    ├─ Record timestamp in RestartTracker [tracker.rs]
    ├─ Check if exceeded per-child limit → RestartTracker.exceeded()
    ├─ Check if exceeded global intensity → IntensityTracker.exceeded()
    ├─ Compute backoff delay → RestartTracker.backoff_delay() [tracker.rs]
    ├─ Sleep the backoff (inside supervisor loop!)
    └─ Call do_start_child() to respawn [runner.rs:136]
```

### Why This Is Friction

**1. Understanding "why did my agent not restart?" requires 4 file bounces:**
- `runner.rs` → was it marked hung?
- `config.rs` → what's the restart policy?
- `tracker.rs` → did per-child tracker exceed?
- `tracker.rs` → did global intensity exceed?

**2. Two similar but different trackers:**

| Tracker | Scope | Algorithm | Configured In |
|---------|-------|-----------|---------------|
| `RestartTracker` | Per-child | Exponential backoff + window count | `SupervisorConfig.restart_policy` |
| `IntensityTracker` | Global | Linear count in sliding window | `SupervisorConfig.restart_intensity` |

Both have `max_restarts` + `window` fields but different semantics.

**3. `restart_all()` duplicates logic from `handle_child_exit()`:**

```rust
// handle_child_exit() does:
let delay = child.tracker.backoff_delay();
tokio::time::sleep(delay).await;
self.do_start_child(...).await?;

// restart_all() does:
for child in &self.children {
    // Similar but subtly different: no per-child backoff, just sequential restart
    self.do_start_child(...).await?;
}
```

**4. Backoff sleep happens inside the supervisor's event loop:**

```rust
// runner.rs:340-345
let delay = child.tracker.backoff_delay();
tokio::time::sleep(delay).await;  // <-- Blocks entire supervisor!
```

While sleeping, the supervisor can't:
- Handle new commands
- Start other children
- Process other exits

**5. No tests for the combined restart path:**

- `tracker.rs` tests: backoff formula in isolation ✓
- `config.rs` tests: policy matching in isolation ✓
- `supervisor.rs` tests: basic restart scenarios ✓
- **Gap**: No test for "hung → cancelled → backoff → intensity check → restart" full path

### Constraints Any New Interface Must Satisfy

1. **Restart decisions are synchronous** — must decide immediately whether to restart
2. **Backoff delays must not block the supervisor loop** — other children need attention
3. **Per-child and global limits must both be respected** — either can veto a restart
4. **OneForAll cascades must coordinate** — can't restart children out of order
5. **State must survive across restarts** — tracker counters persist per-child
6. **Must emit events** — `SupervisorEvent::ChildRestarted`, `RestartLimitExceeded`

### Dependencies It Would Rely On

- `ChildRestart` enum (Permanent/Transient/Temporary) — policy input
- `RestartIntensity` config — global limit configuration  
- `tokio::time` — for delays (but scheduled, not blocking)
- Event broadcast channel — to emit restart events

### Illustrative Sketch (Not a Proposal)

To make the constraints concrete, here's a rough sketch of what consolidation *might* look like:

```rust
/// All restart logic in one place
pub struct RestartManager {
    /// Per-child state (backoff counters, timestamps)
    children: HashMap<String, ChildRestartState>,
    /// Global intensity tracker
    intensity: IntensityTracker,
    /// Pending restarts (scheduled with delay)
    pending: DelayQueue<String>,
}

impl RestartManager {
    /// Called when a child exits. Returns what to do.
    pub fn on_child_exit(
        &mut self,
        name: &str,
        exit: ChildExit,
        policy: ChildRestart,
        hung: bool,
    ) -> RestartDecision {
        // All decision logic here, not scattered
    }

    /// Poll for children ready to restart (after backoff)
    pub fn poll_ready(&mut self) -> Option<String> {
        // Non-blocking; returns child name when delay elapsed
    }
}

pub enum RestartDecision {
    Restart { delay: Duration },
    RestartAll { delay: Duration },
    GiveUp { reason: &'static str },
    Ignore,
}
```

The supervisor loop would become:

```rust
select! {
    // ... existing branches ...
    
    Some(name) = restart_manager.poll_ready() => {
        self.do_start_child(&name).await?;
    }
}
```

---

This is the problem space. Want me to spawn parallel agents to design 3+ radically different interfaces for this?
